    <li> Spending a few extra bucks to be able to shave wet was well worth it. I bought the razor to replace my blades to save money... this thing easily pays for it self in a few months, depending on what blades you&#x27;re giving up.     <li> I prefer blades to electric shavers, but there are times when a quick once-over with an electric just works out better.  This model is a more recent version of a Noelco model I reviewed before. The shape and size are similar, but this one is a bit lighter, has a different color scheme, and is water resistant enough to be used in the shower.  Now, I never shave in the shower, so I didn&#x27;t test that part. The head style is a bit different on this model, but still cuts well. I got shaves as close as the previous model. The lighter weight didn&#x27;t make much difference to me, and the ergonomic shape of both is very comfortable holding it in a variety of ways. Noelco really did their homework on ergonomics with this beastie. It feels good in one&#x27;s hand and is easy to use.  Unfortunately, they still include the pop-up trimmer, which I found poorly designed and virtually useless. Since the last time I tried it I gouged out a chunk of my beard in a dramatically unwanted fashion, I refuse to let it near my face again. It doesn&#x27;t lock in the pop-up mode, and you have to be very careful how you use it. They should have improved it.  Noelco&#x27;s \\&quot;floating head\\&quot; design has always given better shaves than other electric razors, and this one is no exception. I have simply never seen any blade configuration that can beat the three circular heads which pivot independently for moving over the curves and bumps of one&#x27;s face and head. It is the best of electrics.  I have gotten very used to using the other model, and this one has taken its place for now. I still resort to blades whenever I want a really close shave or need to shape my beard, but these models are great for day to day touch ups or that quick \\&quot;need to lose the scruffy look NOW\\&quot; times.  It could be a 4 with a decent pop up trimmer.</li>
    <li> Better than any other razor I&#x27;ve purchased thus far, but leaves behind stubble, no matter how much I attempt to shave it away.  I was expecting this amount of money to leave my face baby butt smooth.  :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But I would still recommend it.  Great battery life.  I can shave several days before having to put it on the charger.</li>
    <li> Update: 2013.04.06: Still working beautifully.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: 2013.02.09: Still shaving just fine. The Philips Body Groom BG2020 and Panasonic Close Curves ES2216PC by this time were both barely shaving any hair by now and would even snag and painfully pull hair. Oh btw I&#x27;m using the Remington iLight Pro IPL6000 which has greatly diminished hair growth so I&#x27;m shaving less.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2012.10.19: I&#x27;ve noticed a just noticeable dulling since I bought it but not nearly as bad as the others I&#x27;ve had. Maybe my finer hair is more difficult to shave too. I&#x27;m still much happier with it than the others.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Review: I bought this one exclusively for shaving my legs and body hair. I&#x27;ve used various different lady model electric shavers over the years for leg shaving and would ultimately be disappointed at some point with the head design, head&#x27;s too small, quickly gets dull and leaves many hairs and stubble, or my favorite painfully starts pulling hairs. This Norelco is not marketed for women but why not? The head design has 3 contour following blades that make quick work of shaving the hair down smoother than any other model I&#x27;ve used. In fact I can shave my legs to where I don&#x27;t feel any stubble.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Notes: Norelco rotary shavers take a little getting used to and you may experience some \\&quot;razor burn\\&quot; until your skin gets used to it but it&#x27;s worth it once you&#x27;re past that if any Norelcos are a little more temperamental shaving right if they aren&#x27;t kept clean. If too much hair stubble is allowed to collect the 3 cutters will get matting over with it and your shave will be very bad. So it&#x27;s best to rinse it out under hot water before it gets to that point. Also if you use it on oily skin that oil will make it hard to rinse clean and you&#x27;ll have to disassemble the head and brush the 3 cutters and combs clean frequently. Another thing is not to shave over long strands of hair or they may get pulled into the cutter and wrap around and clog things so that it doesn&#x27;t shave very well until you pull the head apart and pick the hair out. You&#x27;ll know if hair gets sucked into it because the sound of the shaver will change noticeably.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One WARNING for newbies to Norelcos; DO NOT EVER mix up the head&#x27;s 3 cutters and combs! Seriously don&#x27;t do it! They are precision matched pairs and if you mix them up your shave will not be good! I know because I&#x27;ve done it. Given 2 weeks to a month of use they&#x27;ll wear in and may shave pretty good again but given how pricey replacements are it&#x27;s a mistake you just don&#x27;t want to make! Most of the time to clean the head you rinse it in hot water. Only once every couple of months or more would you pull the cutters and combs out to clean or unclog them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m a long time senior electronics tech who appreciates a well fabricated device and I&#x27;m very mechanically inclined with precision machinery so I consider myself a good judge of the quality of electronic and mechanical devices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;By the way I recently found my old silver computerized Norelco 5885XL from the mid 90&#x27;s that has the big LCD that shows remaining shaves and notifies you when cleaning and maintenance is needed. I totally refurbished it, disassembling and cleaning the transmission parts, and soldering in new batteries. It looks and works like new now and shaves as good as my new Norelco.doesn&#x27;t shave very well until you pull the head apart and pick the hair out. You&#x27;ll know if hair gets sucked into it because the sound of the shaver will change noticeably.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One WARNING for newbies to Norelcos; DO NOT EVER mix up the head&#x27;s 3 cutters and combs!     <li> The AT810 from Norelco is a shaver from the company&#x27;s early 2012 lineup.  It comes in at a mid-level price point with good features, performance, and wet/dry flexibility.  First, the charge on every Norelco product I have owned has been terrific.  This AT810 is no exception.  Indeed, it seems to be the best yet.  You cannot use this product while physically plugged in, for safety, since they do not want to give anyone an idea to stupidly use it in the shower, plugged in.  However, the lack of corded operation is NOT an issue because the battery life is phenomenal, potentially several weeks.  Furthermore, in an event you do run out of power, a quick 1-2 minute charge will give you enough time to complete one shave.  Second, the wet features is a terrific option and a feature that draws in customers  Why not have this flexibility?  Use it in the shower, with a foam or gel, or just with the water.  Pick what you like.  I prefer the dry operation, but I like the option!  The shave is of good quality, but be sure to replace the heads at least once a year for optimum results.  Many are knocking this 810 model as the entire head does not pivot.  The next model up, 830, does pivot, but just slightly.  I did not notice the lack of this feature at first, even though my 2.5 year old Norelco model does have the pivot feature.  I have not noticed a difference in results with the loss of the pivot head.  Therefore, I must assume that the slight pivoting head is more advantageous depending on the shape of your face.  Lacking this feature, does not seem to change the results I get with the product.  Your results may vary.  Overall, a solid product.  I would somewhat agree with reviewers who suggest that for the price, Norelco should have included the pivoting head on this model too.  However, wet operation seems to be the draw factor by Norelco at this new, lower price point, and the pivot feature is reserved for the next model up.  If you can get a good price on the 830, go with it, but you might try this 810.  I have not had any issues with it.  Good product.</li>

    <li> The AT810, as you might have surmised from its name, is the lesser brother of the AT830.  It shares many of the high qualities of the pricier AT830, including solid unibody construction, ability to wet/dry shave and fast charging.  However, it doesn&#x27;t come with a travel case (like the AT830), has just one indicator light for battery charging, and most importantly, its shaving head doesn&#x27;t pivot.  This makes it hard to shave around the neck area; my recommendation is to just pony up the extra $15 and get the AT830, which gives you a better shave around those areas.  I prefer a straight razor to the AT810, and the latter also gave me irritable skin post-shave.</li>

    <li> I do like Norelco shavers, particularly the wet/dry ones.  I don&#x27;t like to shave dry.  Although regular razors give a much closer shave, it takes a long time to get hot water to the bathroom sink, making shaving with a razor and shaving cream impractical.  With the Norelco wet/dry shavers, I can shave in the shower, and be done very quickly.    I should note that I&#x27;m on my third or forth Norelco now.  They stopped making blade refill kits for one.  The batteries of the others have stopped holding a charge.    The batteries are often soldered on to the circuit board inside the shaver, so they are not really user serviceable, and the cost of new battery pack and a repair is really more than the cost of a new shaver, when you consider that the new shaver comes with fresh blades.    My latest was the AT810, which worked wonderfully for a year or two, up until it didn&#x27;t.  For a few weeks, I&#x27;ve had a hard time turning it on.  I pushed the power button, and it would run for half a second, and then stop.  If I pushed the button a dozen or 15 times, it would eventually turn on, and stay on.  I thought that maybe the switch was getting worn out or something.  It seemed to be accepting a charge, as usual.  Today, I went to use it, and it wouldn&#x27;t turn on at all.  The LED was alternating green and orange, as if to indicate that the battery is dead.  I plugged it in, to try and charge it back up, and it&#x27;s still flashing green and orange.  I&#x27;m pretty sure that the battery is gone.  In retrospect, I suppose the problem with turning the shaver on was probably due to the battery not supplying enough power.    I would like Norelco shavers a lot more if I could change out the batteries easier, and they weren&#x27;t so disposable.  I also have a hard time believing that the blade refill packs cost $25-30 to produce, when you can buy an entire low-end Norelco shaver kit for that.    EDIT, 3/20/14:  I replaced the AT810 with an AT410, and last night I started to have the same problem.  Push the button, and it runs for a little while, and then stops.  As far as I can tell, the battery is charging normally, and is fully charged.  I can not get it to run for more than a couple seconds, no matter how many times I press the button.  The Norelco shavers seem to be getting progressively less dependable, and now I don&#x27;t know what to do.  Maybe I&#x27;ll get one of those single-blade safety razors that the Pawn Stars guy is promoting.    EDIT, 9/12/14:  I bought a single-blade safety razor, and the associated wet-shaving kit.  It takes an extra 7 minutes or so to shave, but a 3-piece safety razor is not very likely to die on me again, and $12 worth of blades will last me more than a year.  Oh, and the shave is much much much closer.</li>

    <li> First of all, if you don&#x27;t want a bunch of details, just scroll down to the IN SUMMARY paragraph at the end!&lt;br /&gt;Also- This is a copy of the review I left of the Norelco AT830.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m a longtime Norelco user, and the AT830 is a winner for me. Although I have a tough beard with hairs growing every which way, I have dealt with sensitive skin ever since I was a teenager. I learned a couple of decades ago that a rotary shaver that&#x27;s made for use in the shower was my salvation. Thanks to Norelco wet-or-dry razors, I experience far less skin irritation. For me, having a good rotary shaver in the shower is indispensable. I know I&#x27;m not the only guy like this, so this is a detailed review for those of you who are considering an 810 or 830 model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was glad to learn of the new Aquatec models, having used the Norelco 6000 and 7000 series Cool Skin razors for many years. For what it&#x27;s worth, I tried the last wet/dry model (the 8060X) with the fully exposed shaving heads attached to a single stalk. After using it for a couple of weeks, I found that I couldn&#x27;t get as close a shave as with my old 7735X model with the weakening battery. Also, the lack of a chamber for the clipped hair was inconvenient, so I returned it and went back to the old one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Upon learning of the newer Aquatec models, a friend (who&#x27;s also a Norelco wet/dry fan) and I cooked up a plan. He also needed a new shaver thanks to a dying battery, so we both decided to buy a new model at the same time. He bought the slightly less expensive AT810, while I spent the extra 20 bucks for the 830. The only difference between the two is the &amp;#34;Smart Pivot&amp;#34; system on the 830, and I&#x27;d read mixed reviews as to whether it really mattered.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE TEST:&lt;br /&gt;We each used our razors for one week, cleaned them properly with a good blade wash, then traded razors for a second week trial. We did not compare any notes until after going back to our own new shavers. I not only compared the newmodels to each other, but also compared these shaves to those I got with my 7735X.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, and I tried one extra test once we got our original razors back after week two- I took my old 7735 out of retirement for one last shave. Granted, we aren&#x27;t professional testers, but we tried to stay consistent in our testing. We both shaved just as we always did: in the morning before going to work. Both of us shave in the shower. The highly scientific test was for each of us to see how our shaves held up by 10 pm every night. Before anyone gripes, yes I know that Norelco says you need at least 21 days to try out a new razor. Well, here&#x27;s what we found when we compared our observations after two weeks and two days. Your mileage may vary, as they say.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;RESULTS:&lt;br /&gt;We both found that the AT830 gave a closer shave. No doubt about that; the pivot system did make a difference, since both models use the same HQ8 shaving heads. To be honest, the difference in closeness was greater for me, but I really do have a tougher beard. But by 10:00 each night, I noticed that I had a scratchier face of stubble using the 810. For me, the extra $20 was worth it. On the other hand, my pal felt that his model was fine for him, and he&#x27;s keeping it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And how did my revisit with my old 7735X go after two weeks with the new models? It gave me a longer lasting shave than the 810 did, but not quite as long as the 830. If its battery weren&#x27;t on the way out, I&#x27;d keep that one. However, I really like the fact that, unlike the 7000 series, the new models don&#x27;t require a charging stand. The stand tips over easily and is an extra requirement to haul around when traveling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;IN SUMMARY:&lt;br /&gt;For those of you who didn&#x27;t want to read my lengthy explanation, I totally understand! Anyhow, I found that, with my difficult beard, the AT830 was the way to go. I get a noticeably longer lasting shave than with the 810, and it slightly beats even my trusty old 7735X, which until now,no other razor could do. The 810, however, might be OK for anyone with a beard that&#x27;s not so fussy. Either way, you&#x27;ll get the closest, most comfortable shave in the shower with a good, low-foam shaving gel. I hope this helps someone who really has wanted to know the difference.</li>

    <li> i went to a braun series and did not like it as much as i do the norelco shavers so i came to this at810 love it better on my skin less irritation</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using the AT810 for about eight months now. I had originally planned to buy the Norelco PT730, as I had no interest in the AT810&#x27;s wet shaving capabilities. However, a Black Friday sale made this a better deal, and the one-hour charging time (vs. 8 hours for the 730) made this one worth the slight differences in sale price. And I liked the blue color better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I wanted an electric shaver because chronic pain was affecting my manual dexterity, and conventional shaving was becoming difficult. While this shaver isn&#x27;t really any easier in that regard, it does cut the total shaving time in half (about 3 minutes vs. 6 minutes) so it helps.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver does an adequate job, but I can&#x27;t say it shaves really close. My face looks OK when finished, but feels (not looks, just feels) like I need to shave again after just a few hours. It works well on my cheeks and neck, especially in that awkward place below the hinge of my jaw. However, it takes quite a few passes from various angles to get the curves of my chin smooth. It also seems to struggle more with grey hairs than with brown ones. I think the grey ones are softer and don&#x27;t poke into the holes as easily. My first instinct to deal with this was to press harder, but I found that lifting the heads away from my skin and barely touching my face enables the shaver to get the grey hairs more efficiently.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Though I really have no need for wet shaving capabilities, I did try it in the shower once. It required some soap to lubricate my wet face, and the results were no better than dry shaving. Wet shaving with an electric shaver really seems pointless to me. After all, once you&#x27;ve taken the time to lather up, you really might as well use a manual razor which by that point is faster anyway, and shaves closer, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The pop-up trimmer is handy, and works pretty well to thin my mustache, but the blades are so tiny they don&#x27;t do so well with making a clean lower edge. My Wahl hair trimmer does a better job. Conveniently, however, the pop-up trimmer can deal fairly effectively with most of the longer face hairs that the shaver misses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This shaver&#x27;s construction is solid enough, and after eight months still feels durable. Clean-up is easy with a quick rinse, but Norelco recommends using hot water which negates any energy savings otherwise gained by shaving with an electric razor. Sometimes I just use cold water if I forget to run the hot water. After about six months the shaver&#x27;s performance was declining a bit. It just wasn&#x27;t cutting quite as close. I wondered if the rinsing was depositing minerals from our tap water on the blades. I think my theory was correct, because I started spraying the inside of the heads with a 50/50 mixture of vinegar and water to dissolve minerals, and after a few days the shaver started shaving closer again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line, I give the shaver 3 stars for overall shaving results (i.e. it&#x27;s adequate), and 5 stars for quality construction and ease of use.</li>
    <li> I have a ten year old Norelco shaver that still does an excellent job shaving, but the battery was loosing efficiency. The AT810 does a good job, but not as efficiently as the old one. It seems to shave better when a shaving gel is used.</li>

I wet my face and the razor with just water and the shave was great with no burn and as good as my straight razor. 3. I wet my face and applied a small amount of shaving cream and the shave was spectacular and better than my straight razor.  I have now employed the shaving cream and a little water method for the last three weeks and the shaves are great every day! The Norelco AT810 cleans very easily and the 1hr charge lasts the entire week.  This razor actually gets the beard hairs under my nose that my previous electrics could never get and I had trouble cutting with my straight razor.&lt;br /&gt;  I suggest you try this razor if you&#x27;re looking for a really close shave with no skin burn. It comes with a 45 day free return guarantee so you can&#x27;t lose if you don&#x27;t like it.  I am near the end of the 45 day period but I doubt if I will send this back.</li>

My son uses the water-wash feature but it has rusted some of the steel parts inside, so I recommend using the little brush and a compressed air can (for cleaning computers) to blow out the heads, and washing it only occasionally (and then blowing out the water so it doesn&#x27;t rust).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, it&#x27;s a good shaver. It is hard to make a review about a product that in my opinion is superior to any other comparable piece of equipment, please take this into advisement as you read this review. I have always used Norelco and shall continue. This razor comes with a very reasonable price. It also runs on very little power compared to past Norelco&#x27;s.  I hope this review is helpful in you making your decision to purchase a product for shaving.</li>
    <li> I only give this unit a lower rating because I have had better electric razors in the past for around the same price point. That being said, this unit performs much better than the last one I had... The prior model I reviewed here on amazon yanked and pulled hair out of my face in a manner that was just not cool.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This unit hasn&#x27;t given me any problems at all at this point, I just wish it would do a little better with some of the odd ball hairs on my neck area.     <li> WOW!  technology has sure ramped up since the old razor i got as a handme down from my 80 year old dad.  this thing holds a crazy charge (they say 50 hours and i am starting to believe it) allowing me to travel to south america (220 v) and not need to charge for a month!  it cuts well but i have to work at it... moving over my face many times and never getting it all (dry shave).  but its supremely comfortable and so quiet i no longer have to avoid shaving when my sleeping wife is just several feet away.  i would say its quieter than an electric toothbrush.  its also fully usable wet or even soaking so far as i can tell although its hard to bring myself to submerge it.  cleaning it with water, however, is a cinch.  so, although my previous razors were from the stone age (painful, noisy and couldn&#x27;t hold a charge) this razor is sharp.    UPDATE about how long the blades last: After about 6 months of mostly daily use, i noted a reduction in cutting quality. From the amazing initial cuts that would take a minute or so, now i was getting poor quality cuts in both closeness and number of hairs missed.  After about nine months, i needed to shave for 15 minutes to get a really lousy cut that missed many hairs and was by no means close elsewhere. I tried sharpening the blades with a fine blade sharpener on my own and it got moderately better but did not last for more than a month or so.  Now, about a year after the purchase, i broke down and got new blades online through target (i spent $22 with free shipping and taxes included). With the new blades, I am now getting amazing effortless shaves again.  I also got a replacement policy for 4$ that replaces these blades for two years even with only normal wear and tear. we&#x27;ll see if they honor that in a year... but i specifically told them my scheme (of planned replacement) and they were fine with it.     Here&#x27;s the summary:  its a great razor giving great shaves... but after about 6 months, this course stubble of mine (really anormal beard that if i let it grow comes in real soft) beat down those blades to the point of needing replacement. Philips recommends replacement of blades every year and i suspect its closer to every 9 months. So, factor that into your equations.</li>

The heads take a little effort to pop off, but I suggest you do so regularly for cleaning - while the entire razor /can/ be put under a faucet, that will not properly clean out the heads, and that will cause the blades to dull more quickly, resulting in a less close and more painful shave. Then give it a chance to dry before popping the heads back on.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve always used foil shavers (Braun, Grundig, Remington) when not using blades in the past but I used my Dad&#x27;s newest Norelco a couple of times and figured I might as well give this one a try.  This is a less expensive model than Dad has, but still gets the job done.  What I do like about it is that #1 it doesn&#x27;t try too hard to cut too close, resulting in razor burn and #2 it doesn&#x27;t get hot like most of the foil shavers I&#x27;ve used.  When the foil shavers have gotten warm/hot at the foil is where razor burn was most likely to occur.  As for the negatives, these can be avoided by getting a more expensive model.  The cutting heads aren&#x27;t very aggressive and the motor is weak.  What this means is that some areas will take several passes.  If you want a quicker shave, you&#x27;ll need to step up to a more expensive model, like one from the SensoTouch line.  The one thing I didn&#x27;t realize when I bought this one was that is not a &amp;#34;cord/cordless&amp;#34; model.  I have always bought cord/cordless in the past and would have passed on this one if I&#x27;d realized it was cordless only.  The problem with cordless only is that #1- when the battery fails you&#x27;re pretty much screwed since they don&#x27;t make the batteries user-accessible like the shave heads.  Cord/cordless allows you years more service after the battery fails.  #2- If/when the shaver seems to get weak or not hold a charge, you&#x27;re left guessing whether it&#x27;s the battery or the motor.  Cord/cordless models run at the highest possible voltage when you plug them in so you can tell if it&#x27;s the battery and not be handicapped by a weak battery.  Just plug it in.  It&#x27;s a shame it doesn&#x27;t come with a car adapter, since it would make a good backup/glovebox shaver.  For the price, it&#x27;s not even a bad primary unit as long as you aren&#x27;t too impatient.</li>

    <li> Updated review: My only initial concern when I purchased the razor was that it would not work when it was plugged in, so when the battery goes bad the razor is trash. Well I am happy to report that so far the battery shows no signs of deterioration, and it&#x27;s been a year and a half since purchase. I would still highly recommend this razor.&lt;br /&gt;Initial Review:&lt;br /&gt;I love the feel of the grip and the look of this razor. The cut...well it takes a bit of getting used to. The instruction says it takes 21 days for your skin to get used to the razor and your razor to get used to your skin. If it doesn&#x27;t happen they say they will take it back, I&#x27;ve had mine a week so far and have begun shaving at night so the razor burns have 8 to 10 hours to calm down before I go out in public. Don&#x27;t get me wrong, it&#x27;s not too bad and my lower neck has always been prone to redness from shaving. But so far it feels like it will take the whole 21 days or darn close for me to adjust. So if you buy it be prepared for the break in period. UPDATE: The 21 day break in period is over and as advertised the razor is no longer rough on my skin. I do believe however that the break in period is less about skin getting used to the way the new razor cuts, and more about the razor blades becoming broken in and less abrasive. Either way the result is the same, the razor is working great!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On the plus side: It feels like it cuts really nice and close, and you can feel the blades conforming to your face, so it is as advertised. It&#x27;s very quiet. It also seems to be a lot more gentle on your face if you shave everyday. I&#x27;m a bit lazy so sometimes I&#x27;m cutting 2 to 3 days worth of hair and that probably won&#x27;t work with this little piece of equipment.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On the negative side: It seems like you have to rinse it to clean it and I am used to just being able to shake the razor clean daily and a thorough brush clean weekly. Not this one. The hair seems to want to cling to the inside. I don&#x27;t know but running my hard Florida water over the blades a few times a week seems like a recipe for disaster, what with the blades being $30 to $40. Another thing I don&#x27;t like it is won&#x27;t run when plugged in. I didn&#x27;t know they made them like that. My last shaver ran cordless and plugged in so when the batteries gave out, as they always do, I used it for a couple more years as a plugin. Won&#x27;t be possible with this, when the battery dies, it&#x27;s useless.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall so far the razor seems to perform as it claims, gives a nice close cut, cuts the hair instead of ripping it out, and is nice and quiet. So I give it 4 stars. On star off for not being easy to clean, and the 21 day break in period.</li>
